## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics): velocity-dependent oscillator/forced-damped oscillator modeling
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is an acceleration, and the available state variable is velocity v evolving in time t, which fits a (possibly reduced/embedded) nonlinear oscillator or forced/damped mechanical system where acceleration is modeled as a function of v and time-dependent forcing/parameter modulation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear viscous damping (free decay in velocity): dv_dt = -c0 * v (velocity relaxation when acceleration opposes velocity)
- Constant + linear drag (bias/offset acceleration): dv_dt = c0 - c1 * v (e.g., constant drive with linear damping)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) drag (odd in v): dv_dt = -c0 * Abs(v) * v (high-Re drag where sign follows v)
- Cubic nonlinear damping (odd polynomial damping): dv_dt = -c0 * v**3 (nonlinear dissipation / amplitude-dependent damping surrogate)
- Mixed linear+cubic damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * v**3 (captures weakly nonlinear damping)
- Dry/Coulomb-like friction in velocity form (sign damping): dv_dt = -c0 * sign(v) (idealized kinetic friction; often smoothed in practice)
- Smooth dry friction (regularized sign): dv_dt = -c0 * tanh(c1 * v) (Coulomb friction approximation without discontinuity)
- Pure harmonic forcing (externally driven): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (time-periodic acceleration input)
- Driven with damping (forced first-order velocity dynamics): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) - c3 * v (periodic drive opposed by viscous loss)
- Parametric modulation of damping: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v (time-varying dissipation/gain as in parametric excitation contexts)
- Nonlinear gain/loss leading to self-oscillation in v (Van-der-Pol-like in velocity-only surrogate): dv_dt = c0 * v - c1 * v**3 (negative damping at small |v|, positive at large |v|)
- Rational drag saturation (bounded acceleration response): dv_dt = -c0 * v / (c1 + Abs(v)) (drag that transitions between linear and saturated regimes)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd symmetry in v (terms like -v, -Abs(v)*v, -v**3) typically indicates dissipation that reverses sign with velocity and removes kinetic energy.
- Even-in-v modulation multiplying v (e.g., -(c0 + c1*v**2)*v) implies amplitude-dependent damping where losses grow with speed.
- Pure time-periodic terms sin(c*t), cos(c*t) represent external forcing; their presence suggests driven oscillations rather than autonomous relaxation.
- A time-varying coefficient multiplying v (e.g., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*v) indicates parametric excitation/modulation (e.g., varying damping or effective gain).
- Competing linear growth and cubic saturation (c0*v - c1*v**3) is a canonical signature of self-excited oscillations/limit-cycle behavior in reduced models.
- Non-smooth dependence on v (sign(v), Abs(v)) signals frictional/contact-like effects; smoothing via tanh(c*v) often improves learnability while preserving physics.
- A constant offset term in dv_dt (c0) implies a persistent bias acceleration (e.g., constant thrust/gravity component in a reduced coordinate).
- Rational forms like v/(c+Abs(v)) suggest a transition between regimes (linear at small |v|, saturated at large |v|), common in actuator limits or empirical drag laws.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO3)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v) - c0*beta*v
Candidates evaluated: 57
Matched candidate IDs: [3, 28]
Matched candidates: ["c0*v + c1*cos(t) + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*sin(c6*t + c7)", "c0*v + c1*v**3 + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*sin(c6*t + c7)"]

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the Ground Truth:

**GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v) - c0*beta*v = 0.106257*sin(t) - 0.484397*sin(v) - 0.968794*v**

The GT has three terms: a linear term in `v`, a `sin(t)` term, and a `sin(v)` term.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

**Key basis functions in GT:** `v`, `sin(t)`, `sin(v)`

Any candidate that can match must be able to produce exactly these three basis functions (and no others that can't be zeroed out).

### Candidate 1: c0*v + c1*cos(t) + c2*v**3 + c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*t/(c7*v + c8) + c9/(c7*v + c8)
Has `v`, `cos(t)`, `v**3`, `sin(c4*t+c5)`, and `t/(c7*v+c8)`, `1/(c7*v+c8)`. The `t/(c7*v+c8)` term can't be zeroed without also zeroing `1/(c7*v+c8)` (they share c7,c8). Set c6=c9=0 to eliminate both rational terms. Set c2=0 for v³. Then we have c0*v + c1*cos(t) + c3*sin(c4*t+c5). This gives `v` and `sin(t)` (via cos(t) and sin with phase shift), but no `sin(v)`. 
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2: c0*v + c1*cos(t) + c2*v**3 + c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*v/(c7*v + c8) + c9/(c7*v + c8)
Same issue - no sin(v) term available.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3: c0*v + c1*cos(t) + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*sin(c6*t + c7)
This has: `v`, `cos(t)`, `sin(c3*v + c4)`, `sin(c6*t + c7)`.
Set c3=1, c4=0 → sin(v). Set c6=1, c7=0 → sin(t). Combined with c1*cos(t) + c5*sin(t) = A*sin(t+φ), we can get any amplitude of sin(t) by choosing c1 and c5 appropriately. Specifically, set c1=0, c5=0.106257, c6=1, c7=0. Then c2=-0.484397, c3=1, c4=0. And c0=-0.968794. This gives exactly the GT!
Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 4: c0*v + c1*v**3 + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5*t/(c6*v + c7) + c8/(c6*v + c7)
No sin(v). Set c5=c8=0, c1=0 → c0*v + c2*sin(c3*t+c4). Missing sin(v).
Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 15: c0*v/(c1 + v) + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*sin(c6*t + c7)
This has sin(c3*v + c4) which can be sin(v) with c3=1, c4=0. sin(c6*t+c7) can be sin(t). c0*v/(c1+v) - this is a rational function of v. Can it equal a linear function of v? c0*v/(c1+v) = c0 - c0*c1/(c1+v). This is NOT linear in v. But wait - can we set c0=0? Then we get c2*sin(v) + c5*sin(t). We're missing the linear term -0.968794*v. So we need c0*v/(c1+v) to equal -0.968794*v. But c0*v/(c1+v) ≈ (c0/c1)*v for large c1, but it's never exactly linear. No exact match.
Candidate 15 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 16: c0*v + c1*cos(t) + c2*v**3 + c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*t*(c7 + v)**c8
No sin(v). The last term involves t.
Candidate 16 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 17: c0*v + c1*cos(t) + c2*v**3 + c3*sin(c4*t + c5)
No sin(v).
Candidate 17 verdict: [NO MATCH]
